  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e19bcd7a-6f3c-4231-ae6a-173f5db0ae6b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText3122944117072065725" style="display:none"><i>Revenge</i><br />When Eugenides, the Thief of Eddis, stole Hamiathes's Gift, the Queen of Attolia lost more than a mythical relic. She lost face. Everyone knew that Eugenides had outwitted and escaped her. To restore her reputation and reassert her power, the Queen of Attolia will go to any length and accept any help that is offered...she will risk her country to execute the perfect revenge.<br /><br /><i>...but</i><br />Eugenides can steal anything. And he taunts the Queen of Attolia, moving through her strongholds seemingly at will. So Attolia waits, secure in the knowledge that the Thief will slip, that he will haunt her palace one too many times.<br /><br /><i> ...at what price?</i><br />When Eugenides finds his small mountain country at war with Attolia, he must steal a man, he must steal a queen, he must steal peace. But his greatest triumph, and his greatest loss, comes in capturing something that the Queen of Attolia thought she had sacrificed long ago...</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229569273" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4004792167009451872"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Now I finally understand why everyone seems to like this book so much more than the first. You see, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_' title='The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Thief</a> is a wonderful little book filled with excellent writing, an interesting protagonist, an exciting fantasy world and a great big twist near the end. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40158.The_Queen_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___2_' title='The Queen of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #2) by Megan Whalen Turner' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Queen of Attolia</a> had all of this, but it just had <i>more</i> of everything. It was everything I loved about the first book... on steroids.<br/><br/>Every character and every sentence - <b>damn it, every word even!</b> - is important, serves it's own purpose</span>
  <span id="freeText4004792167009451872" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Now I finally understand why everyone seems to like this book so much more than the first. You see, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_" title="The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thief</a> is a wonderful little book filled with excellent writing, an interesting protagonist, an exciting fantasy world and a great big twist near the end. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40158.The_Queen_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___2_" title="The Queen of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #2) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Attolia</a> had all of this, but it just had <i>more</i> of everything. It was everything I loved about the first book... on steroids.<br><br>Every character and every sentence - <b>damn it, every word even!</b> - is important, serves it's own purpose and is never wasted. This is a characteristic in books that is rare but oh so wonderful when you manage to find it.<br><br>Being told in 3rd person, unlike book one which was from Eugenides POV, allows the reader to see the bigger picture and to better understand the world that forms the backdrop of this series and the political relationships between Attolia, Eddis and Sounis. But, oddly, at the same time I felt like we also got to know Eugenides far better than in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_" title="The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thief</a>, and I loved him all the more in this second installment. He's such a perfectly imperfect character, he's flawed, he's brave without being ridiculously self-sacrificing, he's a little devil and yet you can't do anything but be on his side. Whatever happens to him in the next book has suddenly become very important to me.<br><br>And it's not just Eugenides... I mean, how easy would it have been for the author to make the Queen of Attolia nothing more than a villain sat on a foreign throne? But that's not the story <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22542.Megan_Whalen_Turner" title="Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Whalen Turner</a> is trying to tell. Like I said, Turner doesn't waste characters and her use of 3rd person in this novel lets us readers see the real queen behind that stone mask of cruelty. Of all the qualities I like characters to have, complexity is quite possibly my favourite.<br><br>But I think the book was really sold to me when Turner managed to successfully pull off a romance that surprised me, pleased me and just generally worked without being soppy or cheesy. A young adult novel with romance that doesn't make me cringe? Genius.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="4004792167009451872" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87920704" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13483202220502771808"><b>Update 1/6/19</b><br/><br/>This may be my book soulmate.<br/><br/><b>Original review</b><br/><br/>If I were ever to write a book, this is the one I would want to see my name on. I am not very good at writing positive reviews, so this will probably sound cheesy, but I totally loved every word, every sentence of this story!<br/><br/>"The Queen of Attolia" is a second book in Megan Whalen Turner's series about the Thief of Eddis Eugenides. I moderately liked the first book, mostly for its conciseness and intricate world-building rooted in Greek his</span>
  <span id="freeText13483202220502771808" style="display:none"><b>Update 1/6/19</b><br /><br />This may be my book soulmate.<br /><br /><b>Original review</b><br /><br />If I were ever to write a book, this is the one I would want to see my name on. I am not very good at writing positive reviews, so this will probably sound cheesy, but I totally loved every word, every sentence of this story!<br /><br />"The Queen of Attolia" is a second book in Megan Whalen Turner's series about the Thief of Eddis Eugenides. I moderately liked the first book, mostly for its conciseness and intricate world-building rooted in Greek history and mythology, but this second book exceeded any kind of expectations I had had. It is just so much better than "The Thief" written from Eugenide's 1st person POV. "The Queen of Attolia" is written in 3rd person which allows us to understand the workings of minds of all major players - King of Sounis, Queens of Attolia and Eddis, magus, etc. <br /><br />The story starts when Eugenides is caught by Attolian guard. The Queen of Attolia executes her revenge on the Thief, and in a way that almost breaks Gen. Queen of Eddis, enraged by her Thief's plight, embarks on a war with Attolia, and Sounis starts his attack on both neighboring countries in an attempt to unite the territory against the outside threat of Mede. What follows is a complex story of politics, diplomacy, military strategies and intrigue. <br /><br />I am not lying when I say I loved every word of this book. Because every word of it is important, there is no fluff or filler, every sentence matters. That is probably why it took me 3 days to finish this 300-page book, I simply didn't want to miss anything!<br /><br />But there is more. I really loved the character developments in this book. Just like in "The Thief," we never fully know the narrators. In many ways, they remain anonymous to us, but whatever is revealed, is layered and complex. I enjoyed following Eugenides' transformation from a snarky selfish boy into a strong man. And let me tell you, the romance in this book totally catches you off-guard and certainly pushes boundaries.<br /><br />I can't wait to read the next book - "The King of Attolia" and see where Turner takes her characters next. Why, of why does it take her on average 5 years to write each book?</span>
  <a data-text-id="13483202220502771808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2056958805" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2056958805?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance">❄️BooksofRadiance❄️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062642974" href="/book/show/30363360-the-queen-of-attolia">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68538597-booksofradiance?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68538597-booksofradiance?shelf=near-favourites">near-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68538597-booksofradiance?shelf=ya-fantasy-sci-fi">ya-fantasy-sci-fi</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2056958805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer970334760500663651">Third read in prep for book 6. <br/><br/>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br/><br/>Long overdue for a reread. <br/><br/>Gen, my one and only, we meet again. <br/><br/>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br/><br/><b>I want to climb on the highest rooftop and scream at the top of my lungs - I LOVE THIS MAGNIFICENT SERIES WITH EVERY FIBRE OF MY BEING! but I feel even that won't do my feelings—and this series—justice.</b><br/><br/>Give me a fantasy/fantasy-esque book with heavy political intrigue and you’ve got my undivided attention. <br/>Reading a novel filled with court intrigu</span>
  <span id="freeText970334760500663651" style="display:none">Third read in prep for book 6. <br /><br />~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br /><br />Long overdue for a reread. <br /><br />Gen, my one and only, we meet again. <br /><br />~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br /><br /><b>I want to climb on the highest rooftop and scream at the top of my lungs - I LOVE THIS MAGNIFICENT SERIES WITH EVERY FIBRE OF MY BEING! but I feel even that won't do my feelings—and this series—justice.</b><br /><br />Give me a fantasy/fantasy-esque book with heavy political intrigue and you’ve got my undivided attention. <br />Reading a novel filled with court intrigue, heavy conflicts - more behind the scenes conniving and pulling strings than actual battles, complicated stories full of clever manoeuvres and characters Is. My. Jam! I could never get enough. And given the somewhat slowness of its predecessor, I was not prepared for the magnificent surprise that was The Queen of Attolia. Wow!<br /><br />I felt almost every emotion while reading this. Anger, hate, love, sadness, rage (so much rage) and oh the confusion! Before I even got to page 50 my jaw was wide open with shock and amazement. <br />The more I thought I knew the less I actually knew anything when the whole plot took a completely different direction than I’d expected. <br /><br />And the characters! I truly didn’t know what to make of them. <br />Let’s start with The Queen of Attolia - okay, wow. Throughout the book I hated her. I admired her. I was enraged by her. I freaking loved her and by the end, I was simply in awe of her.<br /><br /><br />Eugenides. What the actual hell. Alright, before I move on, let me preface this by saying, the next book in the series <i>The King of Attolia</i>, put <b>Eugenides on the number two spot of my top five favourite male characters in fantasy. Ever.</b> What a character. What. A. Character!<br /><br />Now, onto the topic at hand, I have never been so damned confused by a character (Confusion, as you can see, is the theme of this review). He was nothing like I’d expected! Especially when compared to the Eugenides of book one, The Thief. It was almost like they were two different people. In a good and a bad way. One thing I did love was that he was not the all-perfect, all-brave, badass protagonist we’re used to seeing who could simply do no wrong or whom no one could best. In fact, he rarely got things right, in this book at least. I was happy to see him humanised and humbled by some extremely disturbing, albeit significant events. He did mess up, got bested at times and he was also painfully vulnerable and weak when the situation demanded it. However, he was also amazingly clever when he needed to be. I love him. I can't say it enough.<br /><br />The plot was amazing and every chapter gripped my attention from start to finish and nothing dragged, nor was there ever a single boring moment. <br /><br />Why some books have to end, I will never, in my life, understand.</span>
  <a data-text-id="970334760500663651" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2030955705" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2030955705" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2030955705?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/34993940-the-queen-of-attolia">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2018">z-read2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=mental-illness-disability">mental-illness-disability</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-series">x-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2018">z-faves2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-relationships">favorite-relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-friendships">favorite-friendships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2000">y-out2000</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2030955705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15384116681536362740"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>If I am the pawn of the gods, it is because they know me so well, not because they make my mind up for me.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Okay, wow, this was... <i>way</i> better than book one.<br/><br/>I love how this one plays around with point of view, showing us both Eugenides’ views on Attolia and Attolia’s view on Eugenides: it’s an excellent view into both of their characters. While I think Whalen Turner occasionally relies too much on not letting you into the head of a character so she can execute a plot twist, we still get</span>
  <span id="freeText15384116681536362740" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>If I am the pawn of the gods, it is because they know me so well, not because they make my mind up for me.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Okay, wow, this was... <i>way</i> better than book one.<br /><br />I love how this one plays around with point of view, showing us both Eugenides’ views on Attolia and Attolia’s view on Eugenides: it’s an excellent view into both of their characters. While I think Whalen Turner occasionally relies too much on not letting you into the head of a character so she can execute a plot twist, we still get an excellent look into these characters, a view that feels dimensional if perhaps not full. <br /><br />The other thing I liked about this book is something I knew I would — <b>
  <u>political intrigue.</u>
</b> Whalen Turner does such a grand job with the power moves, the wars, the intrigue of it all. This one is narratively all over the place, but it is made to <i>work.</i> It feels like a wide story rather than an incoherent one. The plot twists and plot reveals are consistently interesting and often surprising. <br /><br />I also love that the two lead female characters we get in this book are both such powerhouses. And hey, maybe it’s time to talk about badass girls — Attolia and Eddis both make for such excellent political leaders, each in their own way. This book may be led by Eugenides, but I think it’s more about Attolia and Eddis and the power in <b>
  <u>different kinds of strength.</u>
</b> Attolia has lost sight of that in her own power, her own life of ruthlessness. <i>The Queen of Attolia</i> is basically <b>
  <u>a takedown of the idea of petty competition between women</u>
</b> and the idea that there’s only one way to be strong for a queen; Attolia and Eddis contrast so wonderfully. <br /><br />And oh my god, my favorite part of this whole book was Attolia. She is <i>such</i> a good antivillain. We start out seeing her as a complete and total villain, and end seeing her as a very well humanized antihero. Her redemption arc — or, to be more specific, reframing arc — is the best part of this book, and absolutely worth reading for. <br /><br />I mean, I like Eugenides too. He's a mess and a delight. But mostly I’d die for her. <br /><br />Something I did think was missing for me was my investment in the first half of the book; we’re basically thrown into a political situation we only got a glimpse of in book one, and it’s difficult to really get invested in the world and the characters. I also think a few of the plot twists are kind of easy to guess and the time between them too extended. I wished for less lagging between the big moments and big twists. <i>But</i>: I think the conclusion <i>completely</i> makes up for it. This book aged fantastically in my mind; I read this in April and it's August and I'm still thinking about how much I adore this specific book. It kept me invested and I so want to continue with my journey through this world. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>here are my other series thoughts:</i>
</b><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1995733992" rel="nofollow noopener">book one</a> - ★★★☆☆<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2030955705" rel="nofollow noopener">book two</a> - ★★★★☆<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2376881446" rel="nofollow noopener">book three</a> - ★★★★☆<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2467555040" rel="nofollow noopener">book four</a> - ★★★★☆<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2484905696" rel="nofollow noopener">book five</a> - ★★★★☆<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2461451115" rel="nofollow noopener">book six</a> - TBD<br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15384116681536362740" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2082723668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5702335052051418512"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1501983786i/23516362._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>[Edited with my favorite SPOILERISH quotes - hidden behind a spoiler tag, because I'm not a monster]</b><br/><br/><b><u>4.5 stars,</u> rounded up because...well, if you must know, because <i>Eugenides</i></b>. Hellooo, name's Anna, I just finished <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40158.The_Queen_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___2_' title='The Queen of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #2) by Megan Whalen Turner' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Queen of Attolia</a> and my mind is utterly blank. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1501983960i/23516377._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I'd say I'm speechless, but everyone knows that I always confuse talking with breathing so nope, not happening. However I am genuinely sorry but I don't think I'll be able - or even want to - put my thoughts into words this time. First </span>
  <span id="freeText5702335052051418512" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1501983786i/23516362._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>[Edited with my favorite SPOILERISH quotes - hidden behind a spoiler tag, because I'm not a monster]</b><br><br><b><u>4.5 stars,</u> rounded up because...well, if you must know, because <i>Eugenides</i></b>. Hellooo, name's Anna, I just finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40158.The_Queen_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___2_" title="The Queen of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #2) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Attolia</a> and my mind is utterly blank. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1501983960i/23516377._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'd say I'm speechless, but everyone knows that I always confuse talking with breathing so nope, not happening. However I am genuinely sorry but I don't think I'll be able - or even want to - put my thoughts into words this time. First because <b>there are <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229569273?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">many outstanding</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1337482418?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">reviews</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/785887617?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">out there</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1073394504?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">already</a>,</b> given that I'm late to the Gen-is-awesome party ; the second - and <b>perhaps the most important</b> - reason would be that <b>I want to warn you,</b> yes, YOU THERE, you who haven't read this series yet, and who wander oblivious, unaware of the merits of this little gem, <i>you</i>, <b>
  <u>I strongly advise you to stay clear from any review and savor these novels blind.</u>
</b> (she says, after providing links to other reviews... the irony is not lost on me XD) Trust me, the experience will be better (why am I under the impression that I'm some sort of dungeon mistress here, that I do not know). <br><br>If you <i>really</i> need a little more incentive, <u>trust this</u> : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40158.The_Queen_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___2_" title="The Queen of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #2) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Attolia</a> is <b>splendidly plotted,</b> its word is inhabited by <b>characters you will adore</b> and want to protect under fire (when you won't be strangling them, but), including strong women (yes PLURAL), a poisonous snake (I KNEW HE WAS A SLYTHERIN COME HOME GEN BABY) and a minister of war who doesn't know that he's hilarious (to me), the writing... well do tell, what can I say about a writing so compelling that I've read the damn book in a few hours, barely stopping to eat? Huh?<br><br>Now if you would excuse me, I might forget to look at my watch (3:55am, dammit!) and maybe start <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40159.The_King_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___3_" title="The King of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #3) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The King of Attolia</a>, because if you should know something about me, it's this : my restraint is so thin, I wouldn't see its threads if I looked at them in full light, and I'm not one bit ashamed. <br><br><b>My favorites ""quotes"" (more like scenes) are full of BIG spoilers,</b> so <u>don't look at them if you haven't read the book,</u> but aw damn, I love these characters so much &lt;3 <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br><blockquote><i>"Bending over Eugenides, she grabbed his head by the hair above his forehead and twisted. Eugenides's eyes opened, and his feet trashed in panic. Looking up at her, with her face filling his field of vision, he stopped moving as if suddenly paralized. <br>"Goatfoot," she said, "do you understand what is going to happen to you?"</i></blockquote>
<br>I guessed at this moment that she was wearing his earrings, and I was not so discreetly cheering like a maniac XD<br><br><blockquote><i>"Attolia snapped, "You have any mistresses and I'll cut your other hand off."<br>Besides her, Eddis stiffened. Attolia raised her chin to meet the look that her seneschal had said would melt lead. Eddis opened her mouth, but before she could put her thoughts into words, Eugenides laughed. Laughing, he dropped his head onto the bed; then he looked up to grin at Attolia.<br>She looked back at him, and her cheeks flushed. She said, with sincerity, "You are a poisonous little snake."</i></blockquote>
<br>Eeeeeeps I defy you to not smile at this part &lt;3 <br><br><blockquote><i>"I did that next. She said there would be a hunting party leaving this morning; perhaps I'd like to join."<br>"And?" Eddis asked, looking at his arm. He hadn't ridden well enough to hunt on horseback even before losing his hand.<br>"I told her I'd already been hunted in Attolia, thank you very much."<br>"Oh, Gen," sighed Eddis."</i></blockquote>
<br>BAHAHAHAHAHAHA I LOVE YOU GEN<br><br><blockquote><i>"Nooo," he said, and he looked over at her. In his eyes Eddis saw a hint of something she couldn't remember having seen there before. Panic.<br>"I didn't think about being king," he said, his voice hoarse, either from worry or from the bruises around his neck.<br>Eddis stared. "Your capacity to land yourself in a mess because you didn't think first, Eugenides, will never cease to amaze me. What do you mean you didn't think about being king? Is Attolia going to marry you and move into my library?"</i></blockquote>
<br>I'll never stress enough how much I love their siblings dynamics. <br><br><blockquote><i>"What will you do now?"<br>"Oh" - he tried unsuccessfully to keep the tremor out of his voice - "grovel, I suppose."<br>"I've heard you do that before," said Attolia, briefly amused in spite of herself.<br>Eugenides swallowed. "That was begging," he said with a better effort at lightness. "There wasn't much opportunity from groveling last... time." He stumbled, then added evenly, "I am very good at groveling."</i></blockquote>
<br>MY HEART<br><br><blockquote><i>"Eddis looked at her minister, curious. "Your head? she asked.<br>Attolia explained. "He had to be forcibly dissuaded from strangling his son."<br>"So have we all from time to time," Eddis said seriously.<br>One of Attolia's eyebrow rose in carefully conveyed surprise. Eddis took not of the expression, amused to have found at last, she was certain, the original of the look Eugenides had copied. She smiled. <br>Attolia hesitated, then smiled herself, very briefly. In her expression Eddis saw hope for her Thief, and her heart lightened."</i></blockquote>
<br>Damn, there are TOO MANY, I'll need to update this later, because Gen's waiting^^ <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>PS. Am I the only one wondering how old Gen is, exactly?<br><br><u>My reviews for the other books of the series</u> : <br>۩ Book 1, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1237053624" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thief</a> ★★★★ <br>۩ Book 3, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2083617029?type=review#rating_127283259" rel="nofollow noopener">The King of Attolia</a> ★★★★★ [ONE OF THE BEST BOOKS I'VE EVER READ]<br>۩ Book 4, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2084627754" rel="nofollow noopener">A Conspiracy of Kings</a> ★★★★<br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_806430088" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/806430088" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/806430088?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=greek-mythology">greek-mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer806430088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5096435547433247717"><b>$1.99 Kindle sale, Feb. 10, 2019.</b> This is the great but hard-hitting sequel to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_' title='The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Thief</a> (which, fair warning, you absolutely need to read first). This is a fantastic fantasy series, with a strong flavor of Ancient Greek mythology and life. The gods are real and they care, in a remote way, but they can be cruel. My highest recommendation for this series! If you haven’t read it, you’re missing out!<br/><br/>Review posted at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com'>www.fantasyliterature.com:</a><br/><br/>Megan Whalen Turner’s <i>The Queen of Attolia</i>, the second bo</span>
  <span id="freeText5096435547433247717" style="display:none"><b>$1.99 Kindle sale, Feb. 10, 2019.</b> This is the great but hard-hitting sequel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_" title="The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thief</a> (which, fair warning, you absolutely need to read first). This is a fantastic fantasy series, with a strong flavor of Ancient Greek mythology and life. The gods are real and they care, in a remote way, but they can be cruel. My highest recommendation for this series! If you haven’t read it, you’re missing out!<br /><br />Review posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com">www.fantasyliterature.com:</a><br /><br />Megan Whalen Turner’s <i>The Queen of Attolia</i>, the second book in her QUEEN’S THIEF fantasy series, begins much the same as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_" title="The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thief</a>, the first book in this series: Eugenides (Gen) the thief is in prison. This time it is the Attolians who have captured him, but he’s made them, especially their queen, even more angry than he had the kingdom of Sounis in the first volume. From this similar beginning, however, the plot veers in some completely unexpected directions. Whalen Turner explained this in a <i>Publisher’s Weekly</i> interview:<blockquote>I could have written a whole series about fun, cool, exciting things Gen could get away with, but they would all be leading up to a point where he did something he didn’t get away with. The next significant thing that was going to happen to Gen would be when he got caught. It was inevitable. So I started Queen there. I knew some people would be upset but I trusted they would also see it had to happen eventually. To write something else would be a kind of lying to ourselves.</blockquote>It’s difficult to say much more without spoiling the story. This book, even more than most, is one that should be read without being spoiled. The first part of The <i>Queen of Attolia</i> is heart-wrenching and difficult reading, however. The first time I attempted to read it, about a dozen years ago, I foundered on the rocky part of the plot and didn’t finish it. However, after reading the third book in this series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40159.The_King_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___3_" title="The King of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #3) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The King of Attolia</a>, and falling in love with the characters all over again, I came back to <i>The Queen of Attolia</i> to give it a second try, about five years ago. I made it through the book that time and rated it three stars; I was still much more enthused about the other two books in the series than this volume.<br /><br />However, on this read, my third try, I’m rating it a strong four stars. Rereading the entire series, it has become more apparent how cleverly Whalen Turner has plotted this book, how well the books’ plots interlock with each other, and how brilliant and devious her characters are. Small nuances in the plot can carry significance. Each main character has layers and hidden depths. They can be charming and maddening, sympathetic and brutal, all at the same time. And the ancient Greece type of world, with gods and goddesses that are real and intervene occasionally in the lives of mortals, is fascinating:<blockquote>“Stop whining,” Eugenides said.<br /><br />“What?” Eddis’s expression shifted from wary to puzzled.<br /><br />“That was the message. For me, alone among mortals, the gods send their messenger to tell me to stop whining. That’ll teach me to go hide in a temple.”</blockquote>For a young adult fantasy, <i>The Queen of Attolia</i> has a surprising amount of complexity and depth. Due to the painful and disturbing content in some parts of the book, I don’t recommend this for middle grade readers, but the rewards for more mature readers are great.<br /><br /><s>2</s> <s>3</s> 4 enthusiastic stars. Next time I read it it'll probably jump to 5!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5096435547433247717" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3547726763" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3547726763" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3547726763?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=ya-ya-land">ya-ya-land</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3547726763" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4390815465263834755"><a href='https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>THE QUEEN OF ATTOLIA doesn't even feel like it's written by the same person as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3539488197' rel='nofollow noopener'>THE THIEF</a>-- and not in a good way. One of the things I loved about THE THIEF was (Eu)Gen(ides)'s narration. Gen is such a great narrator: he's witty, wry, and through his POV, we get to see the fascinating worlds of Attolia, Eddis, and Sounis. It's written in first person so we get to experience everything through Gen's eyes, and even though the concepts of co</span>
  <span id="freeText4390815465263834755" style="display:none"><a href="https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>THE QUEEN OF ATTOLIA doesn't even feel like it's written by the same person as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3539488197" rel="nofollow noopener">THE THIEF</a>-- and not in a good way. One of the things I loved about THE THIEF was (Eu)Gen(ides)'s narration. Gen is such a great narrator: he's witty, wry, and through his POV, we get to see the fascinating worlds of Attolia, Eddis, and Sounis. It's written in first person so we get to experience everything through Gen's eyes, and even though the concepts of court intrigue and political coups are a bit mature, Gen's narration has just enough humor that he feels young enough (despite being, I think, an older teenager) that a preteen could relate to them. I would categorize THE THIEF has highbrow literary middle grade, like THE GOLDEN GOBLET or THE CAY.<br><br><br><br>THE QUEEN OF ATTOLIA, on the other hand, is narrated in the third person and feels like it's geared towards an older audience (older teens). All of the charming wit and humor I loved in the first book is mostly gone, except as an occasional aside, and the story is much, much darker. In the beginning of the book, something terrible happens to one of the main characters and it's honestly like something out of <i>Game of Thrones</i>. I was so upset I put the book down and stopped reading for a day, and even though I was able to eventually get back into the book, I wasn't prepared for that tonal shift, and I'm sure it would be way worse for a kid to see a character suffer like that.<br><br><br><br>Once I got over my disappointment at the lack of a Gen-focused narrative, I did warm to the story. Turner plots very intensely and there were so many great twists that were carefully planned. It's one of the smartest young adult fantasy novels I've read in <i>years</i>-- everything was done so well, and I felt like all of the characters were developed in a way that felt real. Attolia's backstory, for example, felt like something a young queen might do if she were essentially a captive in her own palace and was willing to do anything to get her freedom back. Eddis was the perfect blend of cunning brutality and motherly kindness that one would expect to see in a queen that ruled with kindness but wanted to keep her throne safe from invaders. And Eugenides's depression was-- well, let's just say that it was warranted, realistic, and potentially triggering to anyone who has ever had a depressive episode or struggled with grief/loss.<br><br><br><br>Regarding that one missing star-- I think this is a book that, despite being incredibly successful and popular, doesn't really seem to have a specific audience. It will appeal to precocious younger teens and adults who love YA that doesn't feel dumbed down, but I also don't think it really seems to be a middle grade series anymore like the first one. I was also a little confused about the world-building because the first book made it clear that this was a Greek-inspired fantasy world, with its own Greek-inspired pantheon of the gods, and yet in this book, Gen is studying Euclid at one point, and the Queen of Eddis makes a sly reference to Helen of Troy. So, what-- do the Greeks actually exist in this world and this is just a made up set of countries that exist nearby them, the way Genovia was a made-up country in Europe created for the sake of the Princess Diaries? It was very odd, and I spent way too much time thinking about that as I read, because I'm compulsive like that.<br><br><br><br>I also felt like ~that one love story~ appeared out of nowhere, and I didn't really feel the chemistry between the two of them at <i>all</i>. I certainly wouldn't fall in love with my torturer and it was really weird and kind of uncomfortable for me. Flip the genders and people would be losing their minds over the abusive plot, and yet because the perpetrator of violence in this book was a woman people are like YAAAASS WHAT A STRONG QUEEN. I never really forgave her for what she did and was not impressed with that ending. I can't say anymore because spoilers but if you've read the book, you know what I mean.<br><br><br><br>Huge thanks to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/19869239-erika-owlwaysreading" rel="nofollow noopener">Erika</a> for reading this series with me. I'm having a lot of fun.<br><br><br><br>3.5 to 4 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="4390815465263834755" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2092918347" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2092918347" />
    <a title="K. Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17568354-k-elizabeth"><img alt="K. Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606078931p2/17568354.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2092918347?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K. Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K. Elizabeth" href="/user/show/17568354-k-elizabeth">K. Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062642974" href="/book/show/30363360-the-queen-of-attolia">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=below-average">below-average</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=boring">boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2092918347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8533470686018698800"><b>2.5/5 Stars</b><br/><br/><i>Well,</i> I gave it a go and continued on with this series, with the hope that my 3 star rating for <i>The Thief</i> would be higher with this second novel. Heck, I <i>expected</i> a higher rating, because people kept on telling me, "The second book is loads better!" And? Was it? Well. To me, sorry to say, but <i>it really wasn't.</i> So, I guess I'm in the minority, once again.<br/><br/>What the first novel in this series had, that <i>The Queen of Attolia</i> lacked, (to name a few) were: lively characters, an exiting advent</span>
  <span id="freeText8533470686018698800" style="display:none"><b>2.5/5 Stars</b><br /><br /><i>Well,</i> I gave it a go and continued on with this series, with the hope that my 3 star rating for <i>The Thief</i> would be higher with this second novel. Heck, I <i>expected</i> a higher rating, because people kept on telling me, "The second book is loads better!" And? Was it? Well. To me, sorry to say, but <i>it really wasn't.</i> So, I guess I'm in the minority, once again.<br /><br />What the first novel in this series had, that <i>The Queen of Attolia</i> lacked, (to name a few) were: lively characters, an exiting adventure, and more humor (I suppose). <br /><br />Even though I wasn't too fond of the first novel, reading this one made me realize that the characters felt more real in <i>The Thief,</i> than in this book. Though, I will admit that Gen was much more developed in this novel. We got to figure out more about him (his strengths and weaknesses), which I really quite enjoyed. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[For example, his depression after having his hand cut off. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <i>However,</i> his improved character didn't make up for the rest of the lot that fell flat. <br /><br />Also, do I even need to even bring up that random romance that just came out of the blue? C'mon. That was so sudden. Wasn't it? I thought so.<br /><br />With the second point, this novel <i>did</i> have adventure, I won't deny that. But it wasn't like the first book. In the first book we followed Gen (step-by-step) throughout his entire journey. But in this novel, we would hear about events that had occurred within lengthy paragraphs or quick conversations. This book just made me think of the saying: All talk, no action. It sums up this novel up so well. There were hardly any real scenes of action (the prologue was the strongest part of the book <i>because</i> the action in it was great), which was something I didn't like.<br /><br />Lastly, this novel was much darker and held little to no humor. While I completely understand why this novel was darker (it wouldn't feel right to be anything else), I just didn't like how different it felt compared to the previous novel. They almost don't feel like they belong in the same series. <br /><br />I don't know ya'll. I almost feel like I'm missing out on something with this series - but I guess it's just not my cup of tea.<br /><br /><b>Overall,</b> I will say there were many scenes in this novel that were much stronger than its predecessor - however, there were also many other scenes that lacked more than <i>The Thief</i> had. So with this I can say, that I <i>probably</i> will not continue this series. Though, I still might. Don't hold me to it. Right now, it's in the air.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8533470686018698800" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_157001697" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/157001697" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/157001697?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer157001697" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6236228776459680981">This was even better the second time around, and I'm so thrilled that I get to see Kamet again in the new book! He really does deserve his own story.<br/><br/><u>Original Review:</u><br/><br/>When I finished reading The Thief, I expressed some hope that the next books in the series would have a faster pace. Well, this is me eating those words. As far as I’m concerned, she can be as slow as she wants! The Queen of Attolia is a book to be savored. It is beautiful and rich, with complex, suffering, gorgeous characters that I</span>
  <span id="freeText6236228776459680981" style="display:none">This was even better the second time around, and I'm so thrilled that I get to see Kamet again in the new book! He really does deserve his own story.<br /><br /><u>Original Review:</u><br /><br />When I finished reading The Thief, I expressed some hope that the next books in the series would have a faster pace. Well, this is me eating those words. As far as I’m concerned, she can be as slow as she wants! The Queen of Attolia is a book to be savored. It is beautiful and rich, with complex, suffering, gorgeous characters that I just want to spend all day with. It is also packs quite an emotional punch.<br /><br />In this book, we finally get to spend time with the <i>real</i> Eugenides. No more false obnoxiousness and bad manners. Don’t worry though, he still has that inner spark of cunning. As the book begins, he is captured by the icy Queen of Attolia, who initially orders his execution but then decides to do something even more damaging. The collision between Eugenides and Attolia sets into motion the breakdown of the fragile relationships between the three neighboring countries of Sounis, Eddis, and Attolia. As the nations start warring, the Medeans stand poised to insert their control.<br /><br />This book has all the great elements of a twisty political intrigue, but I think that at its heart it’s all about the internal battles of the characters. It’s about the devastation that comes when one’s identity is lost, and one must start anew. It’s about the struggle to hold on to the tiny bit of goodness inside, when the world demands so much ruthlessness. It’s about managing to hold on to faith and trust and grace when the whole world seems to be turning its back.<br /><br />It was so completely refreshing to read a romance not based on sappy, goofy, kind, caring love. Megan Whalen Turner presents an honest and challenging kind of love. There is an understanding here that sometimes relationships are built not on easy, careful acquaintance, but by collision, confrontation, and shared tragedy. <br /> <br />It is definitely the title character, The Queen of Attolia, whose struggle affects me the most. I love her cold, quiet, powerful control combined with her inner fragility. I love how her history was revealed in little glimpses that made me more and more sympathetic to her. Reading this book actually makes me like the first book more, because I know so much more of the backstory.<br /><br />Now on to book three….</span>
  <a data-text-id="6236228776459680981" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1337482418" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1337482418" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1337482418?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=book-boyfriend-material">book-boyfriend-material</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1337482418" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6985648208306064801"><b>4.25 Gen Stole My Heart Stars</b><br/><br/>I had a great time reading this with a few friends at <b>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Buddies Books & Baubles</a>
</b><br/><br/>I liked The Thief it was a solid 3 star read, it took a little while to get into but the ending was very solid. The Queen of Attolia though….well let’s just say that it had some very unexpected and crazy surprises in store for me. It was so much better than the first book with complex characters and more than one twist I wasn’t expecting. I really love it when a book blindsides me with s</span>
  <span id="freeText6985648208306064801" style="display:none"><b>4.25 Gen Stole My Heart Stars</b><br /><br />I had a great time reading this with a few friends at <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books &amp; Baubles</a>
</b><br /><br />I liked The Thief it was a solid 3 star read, it took a little while to get into but the ending was very solid. The Queen of Attolia though….well let’s just say that it had some very unexpected and crazy surprises in store for me. It was so much better than the first book with complex characters and more than one twist I wasn’t expecting. I really love it when a book blindsides me with something that I never saw coming and there were exactly <b>3 instances in this book where I had no clue ‘that’ was going to happen until the bomb dropped.</b><br /><br />This series might seem to read a little slower than some other fantasy novels because a lot of the tension and build up is political intrigue and posturing. It is about cunning and sneakiness, who is telling the truth, who is lying and is everything what it seems or something else entirely. I like smart dialogue like that where I’m trying to figure out the true motives and intension of all those involved. I had inklings and suspicions of the actions and reactions of all the characters but I never once knew for sure and to me that is extremely entertaining.<br /><br /><b>The characters and their emotions are complex and intricate.</b> I started this book disliking the Queen of Attolia, shortly into this I despised her, then I grew to maybe feel some empathy for her, to finally possibly understanding her and perhaps maybe now I have an smidgen of like happening for her. It was an emotional journey and I can say definitively that I have a healthy respect for her character. She is smart, cunning, manipulative and merciless sometimes. But The Queen of Attolia is a great three dimensional character doing her best to rule a country full of Baron’s who do not want to be ruled by her and she is so alone.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>There was a shadow behind the wardrobe, a deeper one at the edge of the window curtains. She sat up against her pillows. She pulled the bedclothes up as far as they would go and suppressed a perverse wish to have her old nurse come to chase away the darkness, perverse because she didn’t know if she wanted the shadows to be empty or not. She sat watching until the day dawned and the shadows lightened and were gone.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>Eugenides totally WOWED me</b>. His growth in this book alone is amazing. He is not just the scheming prankster of a boy he once was. He went through some very traumatic experiences in this book and they have changed him. He is different now, but we the readers get to travel with him through that transformation and it is not always easy. This book is sometimes much darker than the previous installment. Eugenides might have taken a little time to bounce back after his tragedy but he got there with a little nudging.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>”Stop whining. Eugenides said.<br />“What?” Eddi’s expression shifted from wary to puzzled.<br />“That was the message. Fe me, alone among mortals, the gods send their messenger to tell me to stop whining. That’ll teach me to go hide in the temple.”</i>
</blockquote><br />I had so much fun watching Eugenides get back on his feet and up to his old tricks. Everyone better watch out, he has a new ambition and plan that I think he was willing to go to the grave for.<br /><br />Eddis is another great character and smart Queen. It is so interesting to compare how similar and different she and Attolia are. Each is ruthless for their people and will do anything for those they care about. They are both smart, cunning and able to see into the true motivations of those around them. But where Attolia is surrounded by people trying to take a kingdom away from her Eddis is surrounded by family, friends and subjects that would protect and keep her in power at any cost. Eddis is allowed to seem softer and kinder because of this but do not let that fool you she is just as ferocious.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Magus,” she said from the doorway. “I’d heard that you had come.” <br />Eugenides swung to look at her. “You started a war in my name without telling me?” he asked. <br />“You will have to excuse me,” said the queen to the magus as if she hadn’t heard. “I overslept, or I would have greeted you earlier.” <br />“Are we at war with Attolia?” Eugenides demanded. <br />“Yes,” said his queen.<br /> “And Sounis?” asked Eugenides. <br />“Nearly,” said Eddis.</i>
</blockquote><br />Being a Queen at war leaves no room for sympathy in most. The battle between the two Queens showed how each used their strengths to maneuver against opponents. I enjoyed the alternating PoVs to get a full picture of the story.<br /><br />I was happily surprised by the direction this story took and I had a great time trying to figure out who was going to outmaneuver who. I think Eugenides wins in that regard though. I think he could test a monk’s patience and get Gandhi into trouble. I’m really interested in seeing what he will do in his new role for the next book. <b>Barron’s Beware</b> Eugenides is coming for you is really all I can think of saying on that.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6985648208306064801" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_95463415" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95463415" />
    <a title="Lightreads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1836077-lightreads"><img alt="Lightreads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1230606449p2/1836077.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95463415?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lightreads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lightreads" href="/user/show/1836077-lightreads">Lightreads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=disability">disability</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95463415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10049843702494815886">Well well! So our pleasant, feather-brained little fantasy romp grew a bigger, bitchiner sequel. Turner made the very good choice of switching from first person to roaming third, and tossed us straight in to political intrigue and war and post trauma.<br/><br/>So – and, frankly, this is one of those spoilers that has to be revealed because talking about the book without it is like talking about Harry Potter without talking about magic . . . this sentence was going somewhere. Since when is drunk reviewing </span>
  <span id="freeText10049843702494815886" style="display:none">Well well! So our pleasant, feather-brained little fantasy romp grew a bigger, bitchiner sequel. Turner made the very good choice of switching from first person to roaming third, and tossed us straight in to political intrigue and war and post trauma.<br /><br />So – and, frankly, this is one of those spoilers that has to be revealed because talking about the book without it is like talking about Harry Potter without talking about magic . . . this sentence was going somewhere. Since when is drunk reviewing this hard?<br /><br />Anyway this book! Which I liked very much, this book is about acquired disability, and identity changed by trauma, and all of that stuff. I reflexively withdraw from books with sudden acquired disability plotlines. I am predisposed for dislike from two directions: I have the lifelong disabled person’s disdain for badly done flailing and trauma and howling and “how will I ever survive I’d rather be dead” (um, you may have heard me <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/91363125" rel="nofollow noopener">demurely mention</a> this on a previous occasion), and at least in the past four years I’ve also had the periodic raw-nerved sensitivity of sudden loss that can’t tolerate acquired disability actually done well. So it’s not that my standards are high so much as that they are . . . complicated.<br /><br />So reading this book and watching myself respond to it was actually really instructive in pinpointing what works in acquired disability stories and what doesn’t. What I liked about this book was that the acquired disability and the post-violence trauma were different processes. People almost never get that right, but they really are. Even when they spring from the same event, and even though they are both fundamentally a kind of violence done to identity, they . . . operate in different keys. They are different necessities to reconcile the old identity with the new circumscribed reality, with what you can’t do now and with what everyone else thinks you can’t do (also two different things).<br /><br />The other thing I liked was that the disability in this book was not about fetishizing pain or woobiness, but instead about fetishizing the person who came out the other side. The former is far more frequently creepy than the latter. And here the process is nicely drawn, with some beautiful moments in Gen’s long, quiet winter in his room, feeling out the new boundaries of his body one tiny increment at a time. And, “I thought I was doing so well.” Oh, yes.<br /><br />Here’s what I didn’t like. I think it is cheap and it is easy for author’s to shorthand their character’s post-disability trauma entirely into their discomfort with the injury being seen. It does make sense – the gazes of others are of course self-definitive, and this is a thing that people go through. But when you channel so much of the aftermath trauma into body discomfort you’re playing with fire. Because disability is not biological. It is not somatoform. Disability is a sociological condition rooted in the embedded culture’s incapacity to, I don’t know, embrace universal fucking design, and the resultant discord it projects back at the disabled person. I realize I’m being all modern social theory at a little young adult fantasy book, but you know what? You do have to deal with the physical pragmatics, but when you get bound up in this idea of body-based disability shame, you’re permanently stuck in the physical and you can’t get anywhere else. Anywhere a lot more interesting, frankly. Also, modern theory is just how I roll when I’m tipsy.<br /><br />So anyway. It’s a book about a smart-mouthed kid who gets hurt, and how he gets up again after, and how it hurts the people around him, and how it hurt the person who hurt him. Big stuff, for a silly little young adult fantasy.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10049843702494815886" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
